Water companies in the UK are employing advanced technology to locate and repair water leaks. They are installing thousands of sensors, such as accelerometers and acoustic loggers, along their pipe networks to detect vibrations and sounds indicative of leaks. United Utilities is collaborating with Fido Tech to enhance an AI system that can accurately identify leaks with over 90% success rate. Narrowband Internet of Things (NB-IoT) technology is being utilized to enable sensors to send more frequent updates to a central server without depleting their battery life. Southern Water has started installing 700 NB-IoT acoustic logger sensors in Southampton, and SES Water is upgrading its flow and pressure sensors to use NB-IoT for more regular data transmission. AI is being used to analyze the increased data volume from these sensors to automatically detect signs of leaks.  Differences Identification: 1. Output (a) uses "AI is also being used to analyze the increased volume of data produced by these sensors to automatically detect evidence of leaks" while Output (b) uses "AI is being used to analyze the increased data volume from these sensors to automatically detect signs of leaks." The changes in VAT rules brought in by HM Revenue and Customs on 1 January are the cause of these measures. VAT is now collected at the point of sale rather than at the point of importation, meaning overseas retailers sending goods to the UK must register for UK VAT and account for it to HMRC if the sale value is less than €150 (£135).  A government spokesperson explained that the new VAT model ensures that goods from EU and non-EU countries are treated the same way and that UK businesses are not disadvantaged by competition from VAT-free imports. The new system also addresses the issue of overseas sellers not paying the correct amount of VAT on sales of goods already in the UK at the point of sale, raising an anticipated £300m every year. Many EU businesses that currently sell goods to UK customers have already registered for UK VAT under existing rules, and HMRC is working closely with those who haven't to ensure they can comply with the changes.
